<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Rheumatoid arthritis</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<tr class="noprint">
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="text-align: right;">[<a class="extiw" href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q187255" title="d:Q187255">edit on Wikidata</a>]</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Rheumatoid arthritis</b> (<b>RA</b>) is a long-term <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autoimmune_disorder" title="Autoimmune disorder">autoimmune disorder</a> that primarily affects <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synovial_joints" title="Synovial joints">joints</a>. It typically results in warm, swollen, and <a href="/wiki/Pain" title="Pain">painful</a> joints. Pain and stiffness often worsen following rest. Most commonly, the wrist and hands are involved, with the same joints typically involved on both sides of the body. The disease may also affect other parts of the body. This may result in a <a href="/wiki/Anemia" title="Anemia">low red blood cell count</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pleurisy" title="Pleurisy">inflammation around the lungs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pericarditis" title="Pericarditis">inflammation around the heart</a>. Fever and low energy may also be present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-1">[1]</a></sup> Often, symptoms come on gradually over weeks to months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Majithia2007_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Majithia2007-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>While the cause of rheumatoid arthritis is not clear, it is believed to involve a combination of <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetic</a> and environmental factors. The underlying mechanism involves the body's <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune system</a> attacking the joints. This results in inflammation and thickening of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synovium" title="Synovium">joint capsule</a>. It also affects the underlying <a href="/wiki/Bone" title="Bone">bone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cartilage" title="Cartilage">cartilage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-1">[1]</a></sup> The diagnosis is made mostly on the basis of a person's signs and symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Majithia2007_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Majithia2007-2">[2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Medical_imaging" title="Medical imaging">X-rays</a> and laboratory testing may support a diagnosis or exclude other diseases with similar symptoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-1">[1]</a></sup> Other diseases that may present similarly include <a href="/wiki/Systemic_lupus_erythematosus" title="Systemic lupus erythematosus">systemic lupus erythematosus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psoriatic_arthritis" title="Psoriatic arthritis">psoriatic arthritis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fibromyalgia" title="Fibromyalgia">fibromyalgia</a> among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Majithia2007_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Majithia2007-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The goal of treatment is to reduce pain, decrease inflammation, and improve a person's overall functioning. This may be helped by balancing rest and exercise, the use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthoses" title="Orthoses">splints and braces</a>, or the use of assistive devices. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Analgesics" title="Analgesics">Pain medications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glucocorticoid" title="Glucocorticoid">steroids</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NSAIDs" title="NSAIDs">NSAIDs</a> are frequently used to help with symptoms. A group of medications called <a href="/wiki/Disease-modifying_antirheumatic_drug" title="Disease-modifying antirheumatic drug">disease-modifying antirheumatic drugs</a> (DMARDs), such as <a href="/wiki/Hydroxychloroquine" title="Hydroxychloroquine">hydroxychloroquine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Methotrexate" title="Methotrexate">methotrexate</a>, may be used to try to slow the progression of disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-1">[1]</a></sup> Biological DMARDs may be used when disease does not respond to other treatments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet2010_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet2010-3">[3]</a></sup> However, they may have a greater rate of adverse effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Surgery to repair, <a href="/wiki/Joint_replacement" title="Joint replacement">replace</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Arthrodesis" title="Arthrodesis">fuse</a> joints may help in certain situations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-1">[1]</a></sup> Most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Complementary_and_alternative_medicine" title="Complementary and alternative medicine">alternative medicine treatments</a> are not supported by evidence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ef2010_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ef2010-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCCIH_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-NCCIH-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>RA affects between 0.5 and 1% of adults in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_world" title="Developed world">developed world</a> with between 5 and 50 per 100,000 people newly developing the condition each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet2010_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet2010-3">[3]</a></sup> Onset is most frequent during middle age and women are affected 2.5 times as frequently as men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIH2014_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-NIH2014-1">[1]</a></sup> In 2013, it resulted in 38,000 deaths up from 28,000 deaths in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GDB2013_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-GDB2013-7">[7]</a></sup> The first recognized description of RA was made in 1800 by Dr. <a href="/wiki/Augustin_Jacob_Landr%C3%A9-Beauvais" title="Augustin Jacob Landré-Beauvais">Augustin Jacob Landré-Beauvais</a> (1772–1840) of Paris.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Landre1800_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Landre1800-8">[8]</a></sup> The term <i>rheumatoid arthritis</i> is based on the Greek for watery and inflamed joints.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paget2002_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Paget2002-9">[9]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Signs_and_symptoms">Signs and symptoms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Signs and symptoms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>RA primarily affects <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joints" title="Joints">joints</a>, but it also affects other <a href="/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)" title="Organ (anatomy)">organs</a> in more than 15–25% of individuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid12860726_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid12860726-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Joints">Joints</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Joints">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rheumatoid_arthritis_joint.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="559" data-file-width="288" height="427" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Rheumatoid_arthritis_joint.gif/220px-Rheumatoid_arthritis_joint.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7e/Rheumatoid_arthritis_joint.gif 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rheumatoid_arthritis_joint.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A diagram showing how rheumatoid arthritis affects a joint</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Arthritis" title="Arthritis">Arthritis</a> of joints involves <a href="/wiki/Inflammation" title="Inflammation">inflammation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Synovial_membrane" title="Synovial membrane">synovial membrane</a>. Joints become swollen, tender and warm, and stiffness limits their movement. With time, multiple joints are affected (<a href="/wiki/Polyarthritis" title="Polyarthritis">polyarthritis</a>). Most commonly involved are the small joints of the <a href="/wiki/Hand" title="Hand">hands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foot" title="Foot">feet</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cervical_spine" title="Cervical spine">cervical spine</a>, but larger joints like the shoulder and knee can also be involved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAVIDSONS2010_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-DAVIDSONS2010-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:1089</sup> Synovitis can lead to <a href="/wiki/Tether_(cell_biology)" title="Tether (cell biology)">tethering</a> of tissue with loss of movement and erosion of the joint surface causing deformity and loss of function.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Majithia2007_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-Majithia2007-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>RA typically manifests with signs of <a href="/wiki/Inflammation" title="Inflammation">inflammation</a>, with the affected joints being swollen, warm, painful and stiff, particularly early in the morning on waking or following prolonged inactivity. Increased stiffness early in the morning is often a prominent feature of the disease and typically lasts for more than an hour. Gentle movements may relieve symptoms in early stages of the disease. These signs help distinguish rheumatoid from non-inflammatory problems of the joints, such as <a href="/wiki/Osteoarthritis" title="Osteoarthritis">osteoarthritis</a>. In arthritis of non-inflammatory causes, signs of inflammation and early morning stiffness are less prominent with stiffness typically less than one hour, and movements induce pain caused by mechanical arthritis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The pain associated with RA is induced at the site of inflammation and classified as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nociceptive" title="Nociceptive">nociceptive</a> as opposed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neuropathic" title="Neuropathic">neuropathic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The joints are often affected in a fairly symmetrical fashion, although this is not specific, and the initial presentation may be asymmetrical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAVIDSONS2010_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-DAVIDSONS2010-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:1089</sup></p>
<p>As the pathology progresses the inflammatory activity leads to tendon tethering and erosion and destruction of the joint surface, which impairs range of movement and leads to deformity. The fingers may suffer from almost any deformity depending on which joints are most involved. Specific deformities, which also occur in <a href="/wiki/Osteoarthritis" title="Osteoarthritis">osteoarthritis</a>, include <a href="/wiki/Ulnar_deviation" title="Ulnar deviation">ulnar deviation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boutonniere_deformity" title="Boutonniere deformity">boutonniere deformity</a> (also "buttonhole deformity", flexion of proximal interphalangeal joint and extension of distal interphalangeal joint), <a href="/wiki/Swan_neck_deformity" title="Swan neck deformity">swan neck deformity</a> (hyperextension at proximal interphalangeal joint and flexion at distal interphalangeal joint) and "Z-thumb." "Z-thumb" or "Z-deformity" consists of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyperextension" title="Hyperextension">hyperextension</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interphalangeal_articulations_of_hand" title="Interphalangeal articulations of hand">interphalangeal joint</a>, fixed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flexion" title="Flexion">flexion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Subluxation" title="Subluxation">subluxation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Metacarpophalangeal_joint" title="Metacarpophalangeal joint">metacarpophalangeal joint</a> and gives a "Z" appearance to the thumb.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAVIDSONS2010_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-DAVIDSONS2010-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:1089</sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hammer_toe" title="Hammer toe">hammer toe</a> deformity may be seen. In the worst case, joints are known as <a href="/wiki/Arthritis_mutilans" title="Arthritis mutilans">arthritis mutilans</a> due to the mutilating nature of the deformities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGraw_Hill_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-McGraw_Hill-14">[14]</a></sup> "Spindling of fingers" of hand occurs due to swelling of the PIP but not DIP joints. "Piano key movement" of the <a href="/wiki/Ulnar_styloid_process" title="Ulnar styloid process">ulnar styloid</a> occurs due to inflammation around the ulnar styloid and tenosynovitis of <a href="/wiki/Extensor_carpi_ulnaris_muscle" title="Extensor carpi ulnaris muscle">extensor carpi ulnaris</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Skin">Skin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Skin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rheumatoid_nodule" title="Rheumatoid nodule">rheumatoid nodule</a>, which is sometimes in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cutaneous" title="Cutaneous">skin</a>, is the most common non joint feature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2013_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2013-15">[15]</a></sup> They occur in 30% of people who have RA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tur2013_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tur2013-15">[15]</a></sup> It is a type of inflammatory reaction known to pathologists as a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Necrotizing" title="Necrotizing">necrotizing</a> <a href="/wiki/Granuloma" title="Granuloma">granuloma</a>". The <a href="/wiki/Initial" title="Initial">initial</a> pathologic process in nodule formation is unknown but may be essentially the same as the synovitis, since similar structural features occur in both. The nodule has a central area of <a href="/wiki/Fibrinoid_necrosis" title="Fibrinoid necrosis">fibrinoid necrosis</a> that may be <a href="/wiki/Fissure" title="Fissure">fissured</a> and which corresponds to the <a href="/wiki/Fibrin" title="Fibrin">fibrin</a>-rich necrotic material found in and around an affected synovial space. Surrounding the necrosis is a layer of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Palisading&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Palisading (page does not exist)">palisading</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macrophages" title="Macrophages">macrophages</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fibroblasts" title="Fibroblasts">fibroblasts</a>, corresponding to the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Intimal_layer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Intimal layer (page does not exist)">intimal layer</a> in synovium and a cuff of <a href="/wiki/Connective_tissue" title="Connective tissue">connective tissue</a> containing clusters of <a href="/wiki/Lymphocyte" title="Lymphocyte">lymphocytes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plasma_cell" title="Plasma cell">plasma cells</a>, corresponding to the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Subintimal_zone&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Subintimal zone (page does not exist)">subintimal zone</a> in synovitis. The typical rheumatoid nodule may be a few millimetres to a few centimetres in diameter and is usually found over bony prominences, such as the <a href="/wiki/Olecranon" title="Olecranon">elbow</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calcaneal_tuberosity" title="Calcaneal tuberosity">heel</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metacarpophalangeal_joints" title="Metacarpophalangeal joints">knuckles</a>, or other areas that sustain repeated mechanical stress. Nodules are associated with a positive RF (<a href="/wiki/Rheumatoid_factor" title="Rheumatoid factor">rheumatoid factor</a>) <a href="/wiki/Titer" title="Titer">titer</a>, ACPA, and severe erosive arthritis. Rarely, these can occur in internal organs or at diverse sites on the body.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>
<p>Several forms of <a href="/wiki/Vasculitis" title="Vasculitis">vasculitis</a> occur in RA, but are mostly seen with long-standing and untreated disease. The most common presentation is due to involvement of small- and medium-sized vessels. Rheumatoid vasculitis can thus commonly present with skin ulceration and vasculitic nerve infarction known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mononeuritis_multiplex" title="Mononeuritis multiplex">mononeuritis multiplex</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other, rather rare, skin associated symptoms include <a href="/wiki/Pyoderma_gangrenosum" title="Pyoderma gangrenosum">pyoderma gangrenosum</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet%27s_syndrome" title="Sweet's syndrome">Sweet's syndrome</a>, drug reactions, <a href="/wiki/Erythema_nodosum" title="Erythema nodosum">erythema nodosum</a>, lobe <a href="/wiki/Panniculitis" title="Panniculitis">panniculitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atrophy" title="Atrophy">atrophy</a> of finger skin, <a href="/wiki/Palmar_erythema" title="Palmar erythema">palmar erythema</a>, and skin fragility (often worsened by corticosteroid use).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lungs">Lungs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Lungs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fibrosis" title="Fibrosis">Fibrosis</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lungs" title="Lungs">lungs</a> is a recognized complication of rheumatoid arthritis. It is also a rare but well-recognized consequence of therapy (for example with <a href="/wiki/Methotrexate" title="Methotrexate">methotrexate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leflunomide" title="Leflunomide">leflunomide</a>). <a href="/wiki/Caplan%27s_syndrome" title="Caplan's syndrome">Caplan's syndrome</a> describes lung nodules in individuals with RA and additional exposure to <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> dust. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exsudate" title="Exsudate">Exsudative</a> <a href="/wiki/Pleural_effusion" title="Pleural effusion">Pleural effusions</a> are also associated with RA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kidneys">Kidneys</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Kidneys">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Renal <a href="/wiki/Amyloidosis" title="Amyloidosis">amyloidosis</a> can occur as a consequence of untreated chronic inflammation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Treatment with <a href="/wiki/Penicillamine" title="Penicillamine">penicillamine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gold_salts" title="Gold salts">gold salts</a> are recognized causes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Membranous_nephropathy" title="Membranous nephropathy">membranous nephropathy</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heart_and_blood_vessels">Heart and blood vessels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Heart and blood vessels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>People with RA are more prone to <a href="/wiki/Atherosclerosis" title="Atherosclerosis">atherosclerosis</a>, and risk of <a href="/wiki/Myocardial_infarction" title="Myocardial infarction">myocardial infarction</a> (heart attack) and <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a> is markedly increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Other possible complications that may arise include: <a href="/wiki/Pericarditis" title="Pericarditis">pericarditis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Endocarditis" title="Endocarditis">endocarditis</a>, left ventricular failure, valvulitis and <a href="/wiki/Fibrosis" title="Fibrosis">fibrosis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gupta_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gupta-23">[23]</a></sup> Many people with RA do not experience the same chest pain that others feel when they have angina or myocardial infarction. To reduce cardiovascular risk, it is crucial to maintain optimal control of the <a href="/wiki/Inflammation" title="Inflammation">inflammation</a> caused by RA (which may be involved in causing the cardiovascular risk), and to use exercise and medications appropriately to reduce other cardiovascular risk factors such as blood lipids and blood pressure. Doctors who treat people with RA should be sensitive to cardiovascular risk when prescribing anti-inflammatory medications, and may want to consider prescribing routine use of low doses of aspirin if the gastrointestinal effects are tolerable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gupta_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gupta-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dt>Eyes</dt>
<dd>The eye can be directly affected in the form of <a href="/wiki/Episcleritis" title="Episcleritis">episcleritis</a> or <a href="/wiki/Scleritis" title="Scleritis">scleritis</a>. Scleritis when severe can very rarely progress to perforating <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Scleromalacia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Scleromalacia (page does not exist)">scleromalacia</a>. Rather more common is the indirect effect of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keratoconjunctivitis_sicca" title="Keratoconjunctivitis sicca">keratoconjunctivitis sicca</a>, which is a dryness of eyes and mouth caused by <a href="/wiki/Lymphocyte" title="Lymphocyte">lymphocyte</a> infiltration of <a href="/wiki/Lacrimal_gland" title="Lacrimal gland">lacrimal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salivary_gland" title="Salivary gland">salivary glands</a>. When severe, dryness of the cornea can lead to <a href="/wiki/Keratitis" title="Keratitis">keratitis</a> and loss of vision. Preventive treatment of severe dryness with measures such as <a href="/wiki/Nasolacrimal_duct" title="Nasolacrimal duct">nasolacrimal duct</a> blockage is important.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>Liver</dt>
<dd>Liver problems in people with rheumatoid arthritis may be due to the underlying disease process or as a result of the medications used to treat the disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Selmi2011_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Selmi2011-24">[24]</a></sup> A coexisting autoimmune liver disease, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_biliary_cirrhosis" title="Primary biliary cirrhosis">primary biliary cirrhosis</a> or <a href="/wiki/Autoimmune_hepatitis" title="Autoimmune hepatitis">autoimmune hepatitis</a> may also cause problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Selmi2011_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Selmi2011-24">[24]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>Blood</dt>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Anemia" title="Anemia">Anemia</a> is by far the most common abnormality of the blood cells which can be caused by a variety of mechanisms. The chronic inflammation caused by RA leads to raised <a href="/wiki/Hepcidin" title="Hepcidin">hepcidin</a> levels, leading to <a href="/wiki/Anemia_of_chronic_disease" title="Anemia of chronic disease">anemia of chronic disease</a> where iron is poorly absorbed and also sequestered into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macrophages" title="Macrophages">macrophages</a>. RA may also cause a <a href="/wiki/Warm_autoimmune_hemolytic_anemia" title="Warm autoimmune hemolytic anemia">warm autoimmune hemolytic anemia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The red cells are of normal size and color (normocytic and normochromic). A <a href="/wiki/Neutropenia" title="Neutropenia">low white blood cell count</a> usually only occurs in people with <a href="/wiki/Felty%27s_syndrome" title="Felty's syndrome">Felty's syndrome</a> with an enlarged liver and spleen. The mechanism of neutropenia is complex. An <a href="/wiki/Thrombocytosis" title="Thrombocytosis">increased platelet count</a> occurs when inflammation is uncontrolled.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>Neurological</dt>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Peripheral_neuropathy" title="Peripheral neuropathy">Peripheral neuropathy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mononeuritis_multiplex" title="Mononeuritis multiplex">mononeuritis multiplex</a> may occur. The most common problem is <a href="/wiki/Carpal_tunnel_syndrome" title="Carpal tunnel syndrome">carpal tunnel syndrome</a> caused by compression of the median nerve by swelling around the wrist. <a href="/wiki/Atlanto-axial_joint" title="Atlanto-axial joint">Atlanto-axial</a> <a href="/wiki/Subluxation" title="Subluxation">subluxation</a> can occur, owing to erosion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Odontoid_process" title="Odontoid process">odontoid process</a> and/or <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Transverse_ligament" title="Transverse ligament">transverse ligaments</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cervical_spine" title="Cervical spine">cervical spine</a>'s connection to the skull. Such an erosion (&gt;3mm) can give rise to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertebrae" title="Vertebrae">vertebrae</a> slipping over one another and compressing the spinal cord. Clumsiness is initially experienced, but without due care, this can progress to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quadriplegia" title="Quadriplegia">quadriplegia</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>Constitutional symptoms</dt>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Constitutional_symptoms" title="Constitutional symptoms">Constitutional symptoms</a> including <a href="/wiki/Fatigue_(medical)" title="Fatigue (medical)">fatigue</a>, low grade <a href="/wiki/Fever" title="Fever">fever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaise" title="Malaise">malaise</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morning_stiffness" title="Morning stiffness">morning stiffness</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loss_of_appetite" title="Loss of appetite">loss of appetite</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loss_of_weight" title="Loss of weight">loss of weight</a> are common systemic manifestations seen in people with active RA.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>Bones</dt>
<dd>Local <a href="/wiki/Osteoporosis" title="Osteoporosis">osteoporosis</a> occurs in RA around inflamed joints. It is postulated to be partially caused by inflammatory <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cytokines" title="Cytokines">cytokines</a>. More general osteoporosis is probably contributed to by immobility, systemic cytokine effects, local cytokine release in bone marrow and corticosteroid therapy.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>Cancer</dt>
<dd>The incidence of <a href="/wiki/Lymphoma" title="Lymphoma">lymphoma</a> is increased in RA, although it is uncommon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Causes">Causes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Causes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>RA is a chronic autoimmune disorder the causes of which are not completely understood. It is a systemic (whole body) disorder principally affecting synovial tissues. There is no evidence that physical and emotional effects or stress could be a trigger for the disease. The many negative findings suggest that either the trigger varies, or that it might, in fact, be a chance event inherent with the immune response.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Half of the risk for RA is believed to be genetic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet2010_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet2010-3">[3]</a></sup> It is strongly associated with the inherited tissue type <a href="/wiki/Major_histocompatibility_complex" title="Major histocompatibility complex">major histocompatibility complex</a> (MHC) antigen <a href="/wiki/Human_leukocyte_antigen" title="Human leukocyte antigen">HLA</a>-DRB1 (most specifically the shared epitope alleles, including *0401 and *0404, although this difference based in race and ethnicity), and the genes <a href="/wiki/PTPN22" title="PTPN22">PTPN22</a> and <a href="/wiki/PADI4" title="PADI4">PADI4</a>—hence family history is an important risk factor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Inheriting the PTPN22 gene has been shown to double a person's susceptibility to RA. PADI4, the gene encoding one of the human citrullinating enzymes, has been identified as a major risk factor in people of Asian descent, but not in those of European descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> First-degree relatives prevalence rate is 2–3% and disease <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genetic_concordance" title="Genetic concordance">genetic concordance</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monozygotic_twins" title="Monozygotic twins">monozygotic twins</a> is approximately 15–20%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tobacco_smoking" title="Tobacco smoking">Smoking</a> may be the most significant non-genetic risk factor<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet2010_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet2010-3">[3]</a></sup> for RA in Caucasian populations, with RA being up to three times more common in smokers than non-smokers, particularly in men, heavy smokers, and those who are rheumatoid factor positive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sugiyama2010_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sugiyama2010-34">[34]</a></sup> Modest alcohol consumption may be protective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pathophysiology">Pathophysiology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Pathophysiology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Both genetic, as well as environmental factors, are implicated in the pathophysiology of the disease. Smoking is the main environmental risk to RA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet2010_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet2010-3">[3]</a></sup> 50% of the risk of having RA is attributable to genetic factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lancet2010_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-Lancet2010-3">[3]</a></sup> No infectious agent has been consistently linked with RA and there is no evidence of disease clustering to indicate its infectious etiology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elsevier_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elsevier-36">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/HLA-DR4" title="HLA-DR4">HLA-DR4</a> is the major genetic factor implicated – but its relative importance varies across ethnic groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elsevier_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Elsevier-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plenge_RM.2C_Seielstad_M.2C_Padyukov_L.2C_Lee_AT.2C_Remmers_EF.2C_Ding_B.2C_Liew_A.2C_Khalili_H.2C_Chandrasekaran_A.2C_Davies_LR.2C_Li_W.2C_Tan_AK.2C_Bonnard_C.2C_Ong_RT.2C_Thalamuthu_A.2C_Pettersson_S.2C_Liu_C.2C_Tian_C.2C_Chen_WV.2C_Carulli_JP.2C_Beckman_EM.2C_Altshuler_D.2C_Alfredsson_L.2C_Criswell_LA.2C_Amos_CI.2C_Seldin_MF.2C_Kastner_DL.2C_Klareskog_L.2C_Gregersen_PK_2007_1199.E2.80.93209_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Plenge_RM.2C_Seielstad_M.2C_Padyukov_L.2C_Lee_AT.2C_Remmers_EF.2C_Ding_B.2C_Liew_A.2C_Khalili_H.2C_Chandrasekaran_A.2C_Davies_LR.2C_Li_W.2C_Tan_AK.2C_Bonnard_C.2C_Ong_RT.2C_Thalamuthu_A.2C_Pettersson_S.2C_Liu_C.2C_Tian_C.2C_Chen_WV.2C_Carulli_JP.2C_Beckman_EM.2C_Altshuler_D.2C_Alfredsson_L.2C_Criswell_LA.2C_Amos_CI.2C_Seldin_MF.2C_Kastner_DL.2C_Klareskog_L.2C_Gregersen_PK_2007_1199.E2.80.93209-37">[37]</a></sup> Related allotypes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MHC_Class_II" title="MHC Class II">MHC Class II</a> and the <a href="/wiki/T_cell" title="T cell">T cell</a>-associated protein <a href="/wiki/PTPN22" title="PTPN22">PTPN22</a> has also been found associated in many studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plenge_RM.2C_Seielstad_M.2C_Padyukov_L.2C_Lee_AT.2C_Remmers_EF.2C_Ding_B.2C_Liew_A.2C_Khalili_H.2C_Chandrasekaran_A.2C_Davies_LR.2C_Li_W.2C_Tan_AK.2C_Bonnard_C.2C_Ong_RT.2C_Thalamuthu_A.2C_Pettersson_S.2C_Liu_C.2C_Tian_C.2C_Chen_WV.2C_Carulli_JP.2C_Beckman_EM.2C_Altshuler_D.2C_Alfredsson_L.2C_Criswell_LA.2C_Amos_CI.2C_Seldin_MF.2C_Kastner_DL.2C_Klareskog_L.2C_Gregersen_PK_2007_1199.E2.80.93209_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Plenge_RM.2C_Seielstad_M.2C_Padyukov_L.2C_Lee_AT.2C_Remmers_EF.2C_Ding_B.2C_Liew_A.2C_Khalili_H.2C_Chandrasekaran_A.2C_Davies_LR.2C_Li_W.2C_Tan_AK.2C_Bonnard_C.2C_Ong_RT.2C_Thalamuthu_A.2C_Pettersson_S.2C_Liu_C.2C_Tian_C.2C_Chen_WV.2C_Carulli_JP.2C_Beckman_EM.2C_Altshuler_D.2C_Alfredsson_L.2C_Criswell_LA.2C_Amos_CI.2C_Seldin_MF.2C_Kastner_DL.2C_Klareskog_L.2C_Gregersen_PK_2007_1199.E2.80.93209-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>RA primarily starts as a state of persistent cellular activation leading to autoimmunity and immune complexes in both joints and other, organs where it manifests. The initial site of disease is the synovial membrane, where swelling and congestion leads to infiltration by immune cells. The various phases of progression of RA are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGraw_Hill_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-McGraw_Hill-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Initiation phase, due to non-specific inflammation.</li>
<li>Amplification phase, due to <a href="/wiki/T_cell" title="T cell">T cell</a> activation</li>
<li>Chronic inflammatory phase with tissue injury, due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cytokines" title="Cytokines">cytokines</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interleukin_1" title="Interleukin 1">IL–1</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TNF-alpha" title="TNF-alpha">TNF-alpha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interleukin_6" title="Interleukin 6">IL–6</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>The factors that allow an abnormal immune response, once initiated, to become permanent and chronic, are becoming more clearly understood. The genetic association with HLA-DR4, as well as the newly discovered associations with the gene <a href="/wiki/PTPN22" title="PTPN22">PTPN22</a> and with two additional genes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plenge_RM.2C_Seielstad_M.2C_Padyukov_L.2C_Lee_AT.2C_Remmers_EF.2C_Ding_B.2C_Liew_A.2C_Khalili_H.2C_Chandrasekaran_A.2C_Davies_LR.2C_Li_W.2C_Tan_AK.2C_Bonnard_C.2C_Ong_RT.2C_Thalamuthu_A.2C_Pettersson_S.2C_Liu_C.2C_Tian_C.2C_Chen_WV.2C_Carulli_JP.2C_Beckman_EM.2C_Altshuler_D.2C_Alfredsson_L.2C_Criswell_LA.2C_Amos_CI.2C_Seldin_MF.2C_Kastner_DL.2C_Klareskog_L.2C_Gregersen_PK_2007_1199.E2.80.93209_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-Plenge_RM.2C_Seielstad_M.2C_Padyukov_L.2C_Lee_AT.2C_Remmers_EF.2C_Ding_B.2C_Liew_A.2C_Khalili_H.2C_Chandrasekaran_A.2C_Davies_LR.2C_Li_W.2C_Tan_AK.2C_Bonnard_C.2C_Ong_RT.2C_Thalamuthu_A.2C_Pettersson_S.2C_Liu_C.2C_Tian_C.2C_Chen_WV.2C_Carulli_JP.2C_Beckman_EM.2C_Altshuler_D.2C_Alfredsson_L.2C_Criswell_LA.2C_Amos_CI.2C_Seldin_MF.2C_Kastner_DL.2C_Klareskog_L.2C_Gregersen_PK_2007_1199.E2.80.93209-37">[37]</a></sup> all implicate altered thresholds in regulation of the adaptive immune response. It has also become clear from recent studies that these genetic factors may interact with the most clearly defined environmental risk factor for RA, namely cigarette smoking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sugiyama2010_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sugiyama2010-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Other environmental factors also appear to modulate the risk of acquiring RA, and hormonal factors in the individual may explain some features of the disease, such as the higher occurrence in women, the not-infrequent onset after childbirth, and the (slight) modulation of disease risk by hormonal medications. Exactly how altered regulatory thresholds allow the triggering of a specific autoimmune response remains uncertain. However, one possibility is that negative feedback mechanisms that normally maintain tolerance of self are overtaken by aberrant positive feedback mechanisms for certain antigens such as IgG Fc (bound by RF) and citrullinated fibrinogen (bound by ACPA) (see the entry on <a href="/wiki/Autoimmunity" title="Autoimmunity">autoimmunity</a>).The debate on the relative roles of immune complexes and T cell products in inflammation in RA has continued for 30 years. There is little doubt that both B and T cells are essential to the disease. However, there is good evidence for neither cell being necessary at the site of inflammation. This tends to favor immune complexes (based on antibody synthesized elsewhere) as the initiators, even if not the sole perpetuators of inflammation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The presence of autoantibodies to IgGFc, known as <a href="/wiki/Rheumatoid_factor" title="Rheumatoid factor">rheumatoid factors</a> (RF), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-citrullinated_protein_antibody" title="Anti-citrullinated protein antibody">antibodies to citrullinated peptides</a> (ACPA) is an integral part of RA disease process. As is the case with many other autoimmune diseases, people with RA have abnormally glycosylated antibodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-immune_glycan_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-immune_glycan-39">[39]</a></sup> It is believed that these glycan (oligosaccharide) alterations promote joint inflammation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-immune_glycan_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-immune_glycan-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Once the abnormal immune response has become established (which may take several years before any symptoms occur), plasma cells derived from B lymphocytes produce rheumatoid factors and ACPA of the IgG and IgM classes in large quantities. These are not deposited in the way that they are in systemic lupus. Rather, they activate macrophages through Fc receptor and complement binding, which seems to play an important role in the intense inflammatory response present in RA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Binding of an autoreactive antibody to the Fc receptors is mediated through the antibody's N-glycans, which are altered to promote inflammation in people with RA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-immune_glycan_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-immune_glycan-39">[39]</a></sup> This contributes to inflammation of the synovium, in terms of edema, vasodilation and infiltration by activated T-cells (mainly CD4 in nodular aggregates and CD8 in diffuse infiltrates). Synovial macrophages and dendritic cells further function as antigen presenting cells by expressing MHC class II molecules, leading to an established local immune reaction in the tissue. The disease progresses in concert with the formation of granulation tissue at the edges of the synovial lining (<a href="/wiki/Pannus" title="Pannus">pannus</a>) with extensive angiogenesis and production of enzymes that cause tissue damage. Modern pharmacological treatments of RA target these mediators. Once the inflammatory reaction is established, the synovium thickens, the cartilage and the underlying bone begins to disintegrate and evidence of joint destruction accrues.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tumor_necrosis_factors" title="Tumor necrosis factors">TNF</a> (alpha) plays a major role in the pathogenesis of RA. There are several theories on how TNF release happens in disease process. If TNF release is stimulated by B cell products in the form of RF or ACPA -containing immune complexes, through activation of immunoglobulin <a href="/wiki/Fc_receptor" title="Fc receptor">Fc receptors</a>, then RA can be seen as a form of <a href="/wiki/Type_III_hypersensitivity" title="Type III hypersensitivity">Type III hypersensitivity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> If TNF release is stimulated by T cell products such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interleukin-17" title="Interleukin-17">interleukin-17</a> it might be considered closer to <a href="/wiki/Type_IV_hypersensitivity" title="Type IV hypersensitivity">type IV hypersensitivity</a> although this terminology may be getting somewhat dated and unhelpful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although TNF appears to be the dominant, other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cytokines" title="Cytokines">cytokines</a> (chemical mediators) are likely to be involved in inflammation in RA. Blockade of TNF does not benefit all persons or all tissues (lung disease and nodules may get worse). Blockade of IL-1, <a href="/wiki/Interleukin_15" title="Interleukin 15">IL-15</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interleukin_6" title="Interleukin 6">IL-6</a> also have beneficial effects and <a href="/wiki/Interleukin_17" title="Interleukin 17">IL-17</a> may be important.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Constitutional symptoms such as fever, malaise, loss of appetite and weight loss are also caused by cytokines released into the blood stream. As with most autoimmune diseases, it is important to distinguish between the cause(s) that trigger the process and those that may permit it to persist and progress.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Diagnosis">Diagnosis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Diagnosis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imaging">Imaging</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Imaging">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RheumatoideArthritisAP.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3436" data-file-width="2100" height="360" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/RheumatoideArthritisAP.jpg/220px-RheumatoideArthritisAP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/RheumatoideArthritisAP.jpg/330px-RheumatoideArthritisAP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/RheumatoideArthritisAP.jpg/440px-RheumatoideArthritisAP.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rheumatoid_arthritis_ultrasound_MRI_MCP_joint_ar1904-2.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1452" data-file-width="1004" height="318" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Rheumatoid_arthritis_ultrasound_MRI_MCP_joint_ar1904-2.gif/220px-Rheumatoid_arthritis_ultrasound_MRI_MCP_joint_ar1904-2.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Rheumatoid_arthritis_ultrasound_MRI_MCP_joint_ar1904-2.gif/330px-Rheumatoid_arthritis_ultrasound_MRI_MCP_joint_ar1904-2.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Rheumatoid_arthritis_ultrasound_MRI_MCP_joint_ar1904-2.gif/440px-Rheumatoid_arthritis_ultrasound_MRI_MCP_joint_ar1904-2.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rheumatoid_arthritis_ultrasound_MRI_MCP_joint_ar1904-2.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Signs of destruction and inflammation on <a href="/wiki/Medical_ultrasound" title="Medical ultrasound">ultrasonography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_resonance_imaging" title="Magnetic resonance imaging">magnetic resonance imaging</a> in the second <a href="/wiki/Metacarpophalangeal_joint" title="Metacarpophalangeal joint">metacarpophalangeal joint</a> in established RA. Thin arrows indicate an erosive change; thick arrows indicate <a href="/wiki/Synovitis" title="Synovitis">synovitis</a>. Ultrasonography (left side of image) in the (a) longitudinal and (b) the transverse planes shows both signs of destruction and inflammation. Axial T1-weighted magnetic resonance images were obtained (c) before and (d) after contrast administration, also demonstrating synovitis. Additionally, a coronal T1-weighted magnetic resonance image (e) before contrast administration visualizes the same bone erosion as shown in panels c and d.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">X-rays</a> of the hands and feet are generally performed in people with many joints affected. In RA, there may be no changes in the early stages of the disease or the x-ray may demonstrate juxta-articular osteopenia, soft tissue swelling, and loss of joint space. As the disease advances, there may be bony erosions and subluxation. X-rays of other joints may be taken if symptoms of pain or swelling occur in those joints.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Other medical imaging techniques such as magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) and ultrasound are also used in RA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGraw_Hill_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-McGraw_Hill-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>There have been technical advances in ultrasonography. High-frequency transducers (10 MHz or higher) have improved the spatial resolution of ultrasound images; these images can depict 20% more erosions than conventional radiography. Also, color Doppler and power Doppler ultrasound, which show vascular signals of active synovitis depending on the degree of inflammation, are useful in assessing synovial inflammation. This is important, since in the early stages of RA, the synovium is primarily affected, and synovitis seems to be the best predictive marker of future joint damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Blood_tests">Blood tests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Blood tests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When RA is clinically suspected, testing for the presence of <a href="/wiki/Rheumatoid_factor" title="Rheumatoid factor">rheumatoid factor</a> (RF, a non-specific <a href="/wiki/Antibody" title="Antibody">antibody</a>) and (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-citrullinated_protein_antibodies" title="Anti-citrullinated protein antibodies">ACPAs</a>, measured as anti-CCP antibodies) may be required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> A negative RF or CCP antibody does not rule out RA; rather, the arthritis is called <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seronegative" title="Seronegative">seronegative</a></i>. This is the case in about 15-25% of people with RA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nishimura_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nishimura-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> During the first year of illness, rheumatoid factor is more likely to be negative with some individuals converting to seropositive status over time. RF is also seen in other illnesses, for example <a href="/wiki/Sj%C3%B6gren%27s_syndrome" title="Sjögren's syndrome">Sjögren's syndrome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_C" title="Hepatitis C">hepatitis C</a>, <a href="/wiki/Systemic_lupus_erythematosus" title="Systemic lupus erythematosus">systemic lupus erythematosus</a>, chronic infections and in approximately 10% of the healthy population, therefore the test is not very specific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGraw_Hill_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-McGraw_Hill-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because of this low <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specificity_(tests)" title="Specificity (tests)">specificity</a>, new serological tests have been developed, which test for the presence of the anti-citrullinated protein antibodies (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-citrullinated_protein_antibodies" title="Anti-citrullinated protein antibodies">ACPAs</a>) (clinically tested using the CCP assay). Like RF, these tests are positive in only a proportion (61-75%) of all RA cases, with a specificity of around 95%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> As with RF, there is evidence for ACPAs being present in many cases even before onset of clinical disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGraw_Hill_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-McGraw_Hill-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The by far most common clinical test for ACPAs is the anti-CCP (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyclic_citrullinated_peptide" title="Cyclic citrullinated peptide">cyclic citrullinated peptide</a>) ELISA. Recently a serological <a href="/wiki/Point-of-care_testing" title="Point-of-care testing">point-of-care test</a> (POCT) for the early detection of RA has been developed. This assay combines the detection of rheumatoid factor and anti-MCV for diagnosis of RA and shows a sensitivity of 72% and specificity of 99.7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also, several other blood tests are usually done to allow for other causes of arthritis, such as <a href="/wiki/Lupus_erythematosus" title="Lupus erythematosus">lupus erythematosus</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Erythrocyte_sedimentation_rate" title="Erythrocyte sedimentation rate">erythrocyte sedimentation rate</a> (ESR), <a href="/wiki/C-reactive_protein" title="C-reactive protein">C-reactive protein</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Full_blood_count" title="Full blood count">full blood count</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kidney_function" title="Kidney function">kidney function</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liver_enzyme" title="Liver enzyme">liver enzymes</a> and other immunological tests (e.g., <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antinuclear_antibody" title="Antinuclear antibody">antinuclear antibody</a>/ANA) are all performed at this stage. Elevated <a href="/wiki/Ferritin" title="Ferritin">ferritin</a> levels can reveal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hemochromatosis" title="Hemochromatosis">hemochromatosis</a>, a mimic of RA, or be a sign of <a href="/wiki/Adult-onset_Still%27s_disease" title="Adult-onset Still's disease">Still's disease</a>, a seronegative, usually juvenile, variant of rheumatoid arthritis.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification_Criteria">Classification Criteria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Classification Criteria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2010 the <i>2010 ACR / EULAR Rheumatoid Arthritis Classification Criteria</i> were introduced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acr-eular_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-acr-eular-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The new criterion is not a diagnostic criterion but a classification criterion to identify disease with a high likelihood of developing a chronic form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGraw_Hill_14-5"><a href="#cite_note-McGraw_Hill-14">[14]</a></sup> However a score of 6 or greater unequivocally classifies a person with a diagnosis of rheumatoid arthritis.</p>
<p>These new classification criteria overruled the "old" ACR criteria of 1987 and are adapted for early RA diagnosis. The "new" classification criteria, jointly published by the <a href="/wiki/American_College_of_Rheumatology" title="American College of Rheumatology">American College of Rheumatology</a> (ACR) and the <a href="/wiki/European_League_Against_Rheumatism" title="European League Against Rheumatism">European League Against Rheumatism</a> (EULAR) establish a point value between 0 and 10. Four areas are covered in the diagnosis:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acr-eular_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-acr-eular-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>joint involvement, designating the <a href="/wiki/Metacarpophalangeal_joint" title="Metacarpophalangeal joint">metacarpophalangeal joints</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proximal_interphalangeal_joint" title="Proximal interphalangeal joint">proximal interphalangeal joints</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interphalangeal_articulations_of_hand" title="Interphalangeal articulations of hand">interphalangeal joint</a> of the thumb, second through fifth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metatarsophalangeal_joint" title="Metatarsophalangeal joint">metatarsophalangeal joint</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wrist" title="Wrist">wrist</a> as <i>small joints</i>, and <a href="/wiki/Shoulder" title="Shoulder">shoulders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elbow" title="Elbow">elbows</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hip_joint" title="Hip joint">hip joints</a>, <a href="/wiki/Knee" title="Knee">knees</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ankle" title="Ankle">ankles</a> as <i>large joints</i>:
<ul>
<li>Involvement of 1 large joint gives 0 points</li>
<li>Involvement of 2–10 large joints gives 1 point</li>
<li>Involvement of 1–3 small joints (with or without involvement of large joints) gives 2 points</li>
<li>Involvement of 4–10 small joints (with or without involvement of large joints) gives 3 points</li>
<li>Involvement of more than 10 joints (with involvement of at least 1 small joint) gives 5 points</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>serological parameters – including the <a href="/wiki/Rheumatoid_factor" title="Rheumatoid factor">rheumatoid factor</a> as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-citrullinated_protein_antibody" title="Anti-citrullinated protein antibody">ACPA</a> – "ACPA" stands for "anti-citrullinated protein antibody":
<ul>
<li>Negative RF <i>and</i> negative ACPA gives 0 points</li>
<li>Low-positive RF <i>or</i> low-positive ACPA gives 2 points</li>
<li>High-positive RF <i>or</i> high-positive ACPA gives 3 points</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>acute phase reactants: 1 point for elevated erythrocyte sedimentation rate, <a href="/wiki/Erythrocyte_sedimentation_rate" title="Erythrocyte sedimentation rate">ESR</a>, or elevated <a href="/wiki/C-reactive_protein" title="C-reactive protein">CRP</a> value (c-reactive protein)</li>
<li>duration of <a href="/wiki/Arthritis" title="Arthritis">arthritis</a>: 1 point for symptoms lasting six weeks or longer</li>
</ul>
<p>The new criteria accommodate to the growing understanding of RA and the improvements in diagnosing RA and disease treatment. In the "new" criteria serology and <a href="/wiki/Autoimmune_disease" title="Autoimmune disease">autoimmune diagnostics</a> carries major weight, as ACPA detection is appropriate to diagnose the disease in an early state, before joints destructions occur. Destruction of the joints viewed in radiological images was a significant point of the ACR criteria from 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> This criterion no longer is regarded to be relevant, as this is just the type of damage that treatment is meant to avoid.</p>
<p>In clinical practice, the following criteria apply:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<ul>
<li>two or more swollen joints</li>
<li>morning stiffness lasting more than one hour for at least six weeks</li>
<li>the detection of <a href="/wiki/Rheumatoid_factor" title="Rheumatoid factor">rheumatoid factors</a> or <a href="/wiki/Autoantibody" title="Autoantibody">autoantibodies</a> against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-citrullinated_protein_antibody" title="Anti-citrullinated protein antibody">ACPA</a> such as autoantibodies to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-MCV" title="Anti-MCV">mutated citrullinated vimentin</a> can confirm the suspicion of RA. A negative autoantibody result does not exclude a diagnosis of RA.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Differential_diagnoses">Differential diagnoses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Differential diagnoses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several other medical conditions can resemble RA, and usually need to be distinguished from it at the time of diagnosis:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merckmanual_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Merckmanual-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Crystal induced arthritis (<a href="/wiki/Gout" title="Gout">gout</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pseudogout" title="Pseudogout">pseudogout</a>) – usually involves particular joints (knee, MTP1, heels) and can be distinguished with an aspiration of joint fluid if in doubt. Redness, asymmetric distribution of affected joints, pain occurs at night and the starting pain is less than an hour with gout.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Osteoarthritis" title="Osteoarthritis">Osteoarthritis</a> – distinguished with <a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">X-rays</a> of the affected joints and blood tests, age (mostly older persons), starting pain less than an hour, asymmetric distribution of affected joints and pain worsens when using joint for longer periods.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Systemic_lupus_erythematosus" title="Systemic lupus erythematosus">Systemic lupus erythematosus</a> (SLE) – distinguished by specific clinical symptoms and blood tests (antibodies against double-stranded DNA)</li>
<li>One of the several types of <a href="/wiki/Psoriatic_arthritis" title="Psoriatic arthritis">psoriatic arthritis</a> resembles RA – nail changes and skin symptoms distinguish between them</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lyme_disease" title="Lyme disease">Lyme disease</a> causes erosive arthritis and may closely resemble RA – it may be distinguished by blood test in endemic areas</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reactive_arthritis" title="Reactive arthritis">Reactive arthritis</a> (previously Reiter's disease) – asymmetrically involves heel, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sacroiliac" title="Sacroiliac">sacroiliac</a> joints and large joints of the leg. It is usually associated with <a href="/wiki/Urethritis" title="Urethritis">urethritis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conjunctivitis" title="Conjunctivitis">conjunctivitis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iritis" title="Iritis">iritis</a>, painless buccal ulcers, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keratoderma_blennorrhagica" title="Keratoderma blennorrhagica">keratoderma blennorrhagica</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ankylosing_spondylitis" title="Ankylosing spondylitis">Ankylosing spondylitis</a> – this involves the spine, although an RA-like symmetrical small-joint polyarthritis may occur in the context of this condition.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_C" title="Hepatitis C">Hepatitis C</a> – RA-like symmetrical small-joint polyarthritis may occur in the context of this condition. Hepatitis C may also induce Rheumatoid Factor auto-antibodies</li>
</ul>
<p>Rarer causes that usually behave differently but may cause joint pains:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merckmanual_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-Merckmanual-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sarcoidosis" title="Sarcoidosis">Sarcoidosis</a>, amyloidosis, and <a href="/wiki/Whipple%27s_disease" title="Whipple's disease">Whipple's disease</a> can also resemble RA.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hemochromatosis" title="Hemochromatosis">Hemochromatosis</a> may cause hand joint arthritis.</li>
<li>Acute rheumatic fever can be differentiated from RA by a migratory pattern of joint involvement and evidence of antecedent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Streptococcal" title="Streptococcal">streptococcal</a> infection. Bacterial arthritis (such as by <i><a href="/wiki/Streptococcus" title="Streptococcus">Streptococcus</a></i>) is usually asymmetric, while RA usually involves both sides of the body symmetrically.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gonococcal" title="Gonococcal">Gonococcal</a> arthritis (another bacterial arthritis) is also initially migratory and can involve <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tendons" title="Tendons">tendons</a> around the wrists and ankles.</li>
</ul>
<p>Some patients are in a situation of undifferentiation (i.e. none of the above criteria is positive), even if synovitis is witnessed and assessed with ultrasound imaging.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monitoring_progression">Monitoring progression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheumatoid_arthritis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Monitoring progression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are many tools available for monitoring remission in rheumatoid arthritis.</p>
<dl>
<dt>DAS28</dt>
<dd><i>Disease Activity Score of 28 joints</i> (<span id="DAS28">DAS28</span>) is widely used as an indicator of RA disease activity and response to treatment, but is not always a reliable indicator of treatment effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The joints included in DAS28 are (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilateral_symmetry" title="Bilateral symmetry">bilaterally</a>): <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proximal_interphalangeal_joint" title="Proximal interphalangeal joint">proximal interphalangeal joints</a> (10 joints), <a href="/wiki/Metacarpophalangeal_joint" title="Metacarpophalangeal joint">metacarpophalangeal joints</a> (10), <a href="/wiki/Wrist" title="Wrist">wrists</a> (2), <a href="/wiki/Elbow" title="Elbow">elbows</a> (2), <a href="/wiki/Shoulder" title="Shoulder">shoulders</a> (2) and <a href="/wiki/Knee" title="Knee">knees</a> (2). When looking at these joints, both the number of joints with tenderness upon touching (TEN28) and swelling (SW28) are counted. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Erythrocyte_sedimentation_rate" title="Erythrocyte sedimentation rate">erythrocyte sedimentation rate</a> (ESR) is measured. Also, the affected person makes a subjective assessment (SA) of disease activity during the preceding 7 days on a scale between 0 and 100, where 0 is "no activity" and 100 is "highest activity possible". With these parameters, DAS28 is calculated as:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prevoo1995_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prevoo1995-58">[58]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<p>From this, the disease activity of the affected person can be classified as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prevoo1995_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-Prevoo1995-58">[58]</a></sup></p>

<td>No improvement</td>
<td>No improvement</td>
